ESCROW AGREEMENT
DATED as of [_________], 2025, made by and between ASSET ACQUISITION
AUTHORITY, INC. (the “Corporation”), a nonprofit corporation duly organized and existing
under the laws of the State of Colorado, and UMB BANK, n.a., a national banking association,
as escrow agent (the “Escrow Agent”), a bank having and exercising full and complete trust
powers, duly organized and existing under the laws of the United States, being a member of the
Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation and the Federal Reserve System.
(1)
WHEREAS, the Corporation is a nonprofit corporation, duly organized,
existing and in good standing under the laws of the State of Colorado (the “State”); and
(2)
WHEREAS, the Corporation has previously entered into certain Lease
Purchase Agreements (the “Leases”) with the Regional Transportation District (the “District”)
with respect to which there were executed and delivered (a) the Certificates of Participation,
Series 2020 (the “2020 Certificates”) in the original principal amount of $63,440,000, pursuant
to an Indenture of Trust, dated as of December 1, 2010, as amended, including by a Second
Supplement to Mortgage and Indenture of Trust dated as of March 3, 2020 (the “2010
Indenture”), (b) the Certificates of Participation, Series 2023 (the “2023 Certificates”) in the
original principal amount of $44,210,000, pursuant to an Indenture of Trust, dated as of
December 28, 2023 (the “2023 Indenture”), and (c) the Certificates of Participation, Series 2025
(the “2025 Certificates” and, together with the Series 2020 Certificates and the 2023 Certificates,
the “Certificates”) in the original principal amount of $89,405,000, pursuant to a an Indenture of
Trust, dated as of April 3, 2025 (the “2025 Indenture” and, together with the 2010 Indenture and
the 2023 Indenture, the “Indentures”); and
(3)
WHEREAS, UMB Bank, n.a. (the “Trustee”) is the trustee and paying
agent for the Certificates; and
(4)
WHEREAS, on the date hereof and pursuant to a resolution of the District
adopted on December 2, 2025, the District is prepaying certain rental payments under the Leases
which will be used by the Corporation to defease (a) the debt service payments for the
outstanding 2020 Certificates that are due and payable in calendar year 2026 (the “Defeased
2020 Certificate Payments”), (b) the debt service payments for the outstanding 2023 Certificates
that are due and payable in calendar year 2026 (the “Defeased 2023 Certificate Payments”), and
(c) the debt service payments for the outstanding 2025 Certificates that are due and payable in
calendar year 2026 (the “Defeased 2025 Certificate Payments” and, together with the Defeased
2020 Certificate Payments and the Defeased 2023 Certificate Payments, the “Defeased
Certificate Payments”); and
(5)
WHEREAS, the rental prepayments provided by the District will be used
to pay the Defeased Certificate Payments on their regular schedule payment dates, all as set forth
in the certified public accountant's report attached as Exhibit 1 to this Escrow Agreement (the
“Defeased Certificate Payment Requirements”); and
(6)
WHEREAS, the Corporation, by a resolution adopted by the Corporation
on December ___, 2025 (the “Resolution”), has:

NOW, THEREFORE, THIS ESCROW AGREEMENT WITNESSETH:
That in consideration of the premises and the mutual agreements herein contained,
and in order to secure the payment of the Defeased Certificate Payment Requirements as the
same become due, the parties hereto mutually undertake, promise and agree for themselves and
their respective representatives, successors and assigns, as follows:
Section 1.

Creation of Escrow.

A.
On the date hereof there shall be purchased, with $__________ of legally
available funds provided by the District, the Federal Securities (as defined in the Indentures)
shown in Exhibit 1 to this Escrow Agreement (the “Initial Federal Securities”) and the Initial

1.D.5.b

Federal Securities and an initial cash deposit of $__________ (the “initial deposit”) shall be
credited to and accounted for in a separate trust account designated as the “Defeased Certificate
of Participation Payments, Escrow Account” (the “Escrow Account”). Receipt of $__________
by the Escrow Agent to be applied as provided herein is hereby acknowledged.
B.
To the extent such action is not inconsistent herewith or with the
Indentures, other Federal Securities may be substituted for the Initial Federal Securities if such
Initial Federal Securities are unavailable for purchase on the date hereof or other Federal
Securities may be substituted for any Federal Securities held in the Escrow Account if such
substitution is required or permitted by Section 148 of the Internal Revenue Code of 1986, as
amended (the “Tax Code”), and the applicable regulations thereunder, subject in any case to
sufficiency demonstrations and yield proofs in a certified public accountant's report, and subject
to a favorable opinion of the District's special counsel as to the legality of any such substitution,
and the continued exemption of interest on the Certificates from federal income taxation (except
certain alternative minimum taxes described in special counsel's opinion), and in any event in
such a manner so as not to increase the price paid for the initial acquisition of Federal Securities
for the Escrow Account. The certified public accountant's report must indicate that the receipts
from the substitute securities are sufficient without any need for reinvestment to fully pay the
Defeased Certificate Payment Requirements. In lieu of, or in addition to, substituting other
Federal Securities pursuant to the preceding sentence, moneys in an amount equal to the
principal of and interest on all or any portion of such Initial Federal Securities may be credited to
the Escrow Account subject to the provisions of Section 5 hereof. Any such cash shall be
deemed to be part of the initial deposit. Any Federal Securities temporarily substituted may be
withdrawn from the Escrow Account when the Initial Federal Securities are purchased and
credited to the Escrow Account. Similarly, any temporary advancement of moneys to the
Escrow Account to pay designated Defeased Certificate Payment Requirements, because of a
failure to receive promptly the principal of and interest on any Federal Securities at their
respective fixed maturity dates, or otherwise, may be repaid to the person advancing such
moneys upon the receipt by the Escrow Agent of such principal and interest payments on such
Federal Securities.
C.
The initial deposit, the proceeds of the Initial Federal Securities (and of
any other Federal Securities acquired as an investment or reinvestment of moneys accounted for
in the Escrow Account), and any such Federal Securities themselves (other than Federal
Securities, including the Initial Federal Securities, held as book-entries) shall be deposited with
the Escrow Agent and credited to and accounted for in the Escrow Account. The securities and
moneys accounted for therein shall be redeemed and paid out and otherwise administered by the
Escrow Agent for the benefit of the District and the owners of the Certificates as provided in this
Escrow Agreement and the Indentures.
Section 2.

Purpose of Escrow.

A.
The Escrow Agent shall hold the initial deposit, all Federal Securities
accounted for in the Escrow Account (other than any Federal Securities, including the Initial
Federal Securities, held as book-entries), and all moneys received from time to time as interest
on and principal of such Federal Securities (including those held as book-entries), in trust to

Attachment: 2026 Debt Service Defeasance - Certificates of Participation - Escrow Agreement (5225 : 2026 Debt Service Defeasance -

1.D.5.b

-3\\4160-0290-6976 v5

Packet Pg. 209

secure and for the payment of the Defeased Certificate Payment Requirements, as the same
become due.
B.
Except as provided in paragraph B of Section 1 and in Section 8 hereof,
the Escrow Agent shall collect the principal of and interest on such Federal Securities promptly
as such principal and interest become due and shall apply all money so collected to the payment
of the Defeased Certificate Payment Requirements as aforesaid.
Section 3.

Accounting for Escrow.

A.
The moneys and the Federal Securities accounted for in the Escrow
Account shall not be subject to checks drawn by the Corporation or the District or otherwise
subject to the order of the Corporation or the District except as otherwise provided in
paragraph B of Section 1 and in Section 8 hereof.
B.
From amounts on deposit in the Escrow Account, the Escrow Agent shall
make the transfers required by Section 7 hereof to permit the payment, without any default, of
the Defeased Certificate Payment Requirements as the same become due.
C.
Except as otherwise provided in paragraph B of Section 1 hereof, there
shall be no sale of any Federal Securities held hereunder, and no Federal Securities held
hereunder and callable for prior redemption at the District's option shall be called at any time for
prior redemption, except if necessary to avoid a default in the payment of the Defeased
Certificate Payment Requirements.
Section 4.

Maturities of Federal Securities.

A.
Federal Securities shall not be callable by the issuer thereof and shall be
purchased in such manner:
(1)
So that such Federal Securities may be redeemed in due season at
their respective maturities to meet the Defeased Certificate Payment Requirements as the
same become due; and
(2)
So that any sale or prior redemption of such Federal Securities
shall be unnecessary.
B.
There shall be no substitution of any Federal Securities except as
otherwise provided in paragraph B of Section 1 hereof.
Section 5.

Reinvestments.

A.
The Escrow Agent shall reinvest the cash balances listed in Exhibit 1
(including Exhibit A therein) for the period designated therein, if any, in state and local
government series securities (“slgs”) purchased directly from the United States Government by
the Escrow Agent in the name of the District. All of the slgs in which such reinvestments are
made shall bear interest at the rate of zero percent (0%) per annum. The Escrow Agent agrees to
comply with Part 344 of Title 31, Code of Federal Regulations, and with such other regulations

Attachment: 2026 Debt Service Defeasance - Certificates of Participation - Escrow Agreement (5225 : 2026 Debt Service Defeasance -

1.D.5.b

-4\\4160-0290-6976 v5

Packet Pg. 210

of the United States Treasury, Bureau of Public Debt, as are from time to time in effect in
subscribing for and purchasing such slgs, including without limitation, requirements with respect
to submitting subscriptions to a Federal Reserve Bank or Branch in advance of the date of
purchase of the slgs.
B.
In addition to or, as the case may be, in lieu of the reinvestments required
by paragraph A of this Section, the Escrow Agent, at the written direction of the Corporation,
shall invest the initial cash, if any, and shall reinvest in Federal Securities any moneys received
in payment of the principal of and interest on any Federal Securities accounted for in the Escrow
Account. The Corporation’s direction shall be subject to the limitations of Sections 1, 4 and 6
hereof and the following limitations. In providing written direction to the Escrow Agent, the
Corporation certifies that the investment does not fail to comply with any limitations of Sections
1, 4, 6, or as follows:
(1)
Any such Federal Securities shall not be subject to redemption
prior to their respective maturities at the option of their issuer.
(2)
Any such Federal Securities shall mature on or prior to the date
when the proceeds thereof must be available for the prompt payment of the Defeased
Certificate Payment Requirements, as the same become due.
(3)
Under no circumstances shall any reinvestment be made under this
Section if such reinvestment, alone or in combination with any other investment or
reinvestment, violates the applicable provisions of Section 148 of the Tax Code, and the
rules and regulations thereunder.
(4)
The District shall have furnished to the Escrow Agent a written
opinion of the District's special counsel to the effect that such reinvestment, as described
in the opinion, complies with subparagraph B(3) of this Section.
Section 6.
Sufficiency of Escrow. The moneys and Federal Securities
accounted for in the Escrow Account shall be in an amount (or have appropriate maturities and
yields to produce an amount) which at all times shall be sufficient to pay the Defeased Certificate
Payment Requirements as they become due.
Section 7.
Transfers for Defeased Certificate Payment Requirements.
The Escrow Agent shall make such credit arrangements and transfers to the trustee for the
Certificates (the “Trustee”) as will assure, to the extent of money in the Escrow Account
properly allocable to and available therefor, the timely payment of the Defeased Certificate
Payment Requirements when due. The Escrow Agent shall not be responsible for the sufficiency
of the Escrow Account.
Section 8.
Termination of Escrow Account. When payment or provisions
for payment shall have been made so that all Defeased Certificate Payment Requirements shall
have been paid in full and discharged, the Escrow Agent shall immediately pay over to the
District the moneys, if any, then remaining in the Escrow Account and shall make forthwith a
final report to the District and the Corporation. Such moneys may be used by the District for any
lawful purpose, subject to any limitations in the Indentures.

Section 10.

Character of Deposit.

A.
It is recognized that title to the Federal Securities and money accounted
for in the Escrow Account from time to time shall remain vested in the Corporation or in the
Escrow Agent on behalf of the Corporation but subject always to the prior charge and lien
thereon of this Escrow Agreement and the use thereof required to be made by the provisions of
this Escrow Agreement and the Indentures.
B.
The Escrow Agent shall hold all such Federal Securities (except as they
may be held as book-entries) and money in the Escrow Account as a special escrow fund, which
is accounted for separately and shall never commingle such securities or money with other
securities or money in non-trust areas of the Escrow Agent.
Section 11.

Securing Deposit.

A.

Escrow Account to be registered in the name of the Escrow Agent on behalf of the Corporation
for payment, if they are registrable for payment, and in such event shall obtain the necessary
endorsements from the duly authorized officials of the Corporation as they become due.
B.
The Corporation, in connection with any Federal Securities accounted for
in the Escrow Account and held as book-entries, shall cooperate with the Escrow Agent and shall
forthwith make arrangements with an appropriate representative of the issuer of such Federal
Securities so that the interest on and the principal of the Federal Securities shall be promptly
transmitted, as the same become due from time to time, to the Escrow Agent.
C.
All uninvested money held at any time in the Escrow Account shall be
continuously secured by the deposit of Federal Securities, as directed in writing by the
Corporation, in a principal amount and value always not less than the total amount of uninvested
money in the Escrow Account:
(1)

In any branch of the Federal Reserve Bank; or

(2)

In any commercial bank which:

Section 12.

Notices.

The Escrow Agent, on behalf of the Corporation, shall, as soon as practicable

notice of the defeasance of the Defeased Certificate Payments to the extent required in
accordance with the Indentures. Forms of such notices of prior redemption and defeasance are
attached hereto as Exhibit 6.
Section 13.

Irrevocability and Amendment.

A.
Except as herein provided this Escrow Agreement shall be irrevocable and
not subject to amendment.
B.
The provisions of this Escrow Agreement may be amended, waived or
modified upon approval of the owners of all of the then outstanding Certificates. The provisions
of this Escrow Agreement also may be amended, waived or modified without the approval of
such owners for one or more of the following purposes:
(1)
to cure any ambiguity, or to cure, correct or supplement any formal
defect or omission or inconsistent provision contained in this Escrow Agreement;
(2)
to pledge additional revenues, properties or collateral as security
for the Certificates; or
(3)

to deposit additional moneys or Federal Securities into the Escrow

Account.
Notwithstanding any other provision hereof, no amendment, modification or
waiver shall be effective if it is materially prejudicial to the owners of the Certificates or affects
the exclusion of the interest on the Certificates from gross income for federal income tax
purposes, unless such amendment, waiver or modification is approved by the owners of all of the
then outstanding Certificates affected thereby. The Escrow Agent shall be entitled to rely
exclusively upon an unqualified written opinion of nationally recognized bond counsel with
respect to compliance with this Section, including the extent, if any, to which any amendment,
modification or waiver is materially prejudicial to the owners of the Certificates or if it affects
the exclusion of the interest on the Certificates from gross income for federal income tax

Section 14.

Exculpatory Provisions.

A.
The duties and responsibilities of the Escrow Agent are limited to those
expressly and specifically stated in this Escrow Agreement.
B.
The Escrow Agent shall not be liable or responsible for any loss resulting
from any investment or reinvestment made pursuant to this Escrow Agreement and made in
compliance with the provisions hereof.
C.
The Escrow Agent shall not be liable for any act done or step taken or
omitted by it or for any mistake of fact or law or for anything which it may do or refrain from
doing, except for its gross negligence or willful misconduct.
D.
The Escrow Agent shall neither be under any obligation to inquire into or
be in any way responsible for the performance or nonperformance by the Corporation of any of
its obligations contained in this Escrow Agreement, nor shall the Escrow Agent be responsible in
any manner for the recitals or statements in the Resolution, in the Indentures, in the Certificates,
or in any proceedings taken in connection therewith (other than its responsibilities as trustee
under such instruments.
E.
Nothing in this Escrow Agreement creates any obligation or liabilities on
the part of the Escrow Agent to anyone other than the Corporation, the District and the owners of
the Certificates.
F.
The Escrow Agent shall not be liable for the accuracy of the calculations
in the certified public accountant's report as to the sufficiency of the proceeds of the Federal
Securities and moneys to pay the Defeased Certificate Payment Requirements. So long as the
Escrow Agent applies the proceeds of the Federal Securities and moneys held in the Escrow
Account and timely gives or causes the notices of defeasance to be given as provided herein, the
Escrow Agent shall not be liable for any deficiencies in the amounts necessary to pay the
Defeased Certificate Payment Requirements. The foregoing provisions of this Subsection 14(F)
are, however, not intended and shall not be construed to release the Escrow Agent for exercising
due care in the circumstances presented from time to time.
G.
The Escrow Agent may consult with counsel as reasonably necessary, and
the advice or opinion of such counsel shall be full and complete authorization and protection in
respect of any action taken or suffered by it in good faith and in accordance therewith. In the
absence of its gross negligence or willful misconduct, the Escrow Agent may rely conclusively
upon the truth, completeness and accuracy of the statements, certificates, opinions, resolutions
and other documents conforming to the requirements of this Escrow Agreement. The Escrow
Agent shall be under no obligation to institute any suit or action or other proceeding under this
Agreement or to enter any appearance in any suit, action or proceeding in which it may be
defendant or to take any steps in the enforcement of its, or any, rights and powers hereunder, nor
shall be deemed to have failed to take any such action, unless and until it shall have been
indemnified by the District to its satisfaction against any and all costs and expenses, outlays,

counsel fees and other disbursements, including its own reasonable fees, and if any judgment,
decree or recovery be obtained by the Escrow Agent, payment of all sums due it, as aforesaid,
shall be a first charge against the amount of any such judgment, decree or recovery.
Section 15. Time of Essence. Time is of the essence in the performance of the
obligations from time to time imposed upon the Escrow Agent by this Escrow Agreement.
Section 16.

Successors.

A.
Whenever in this Escrow Agreement the Corporation or the Escrow Agent
is named or is referred to, such provision is deemed to include any successor of the Corporation
or the Escrow Agent, respectively, immediate or intermediate, whether so expressed or not.
B.
All of the stipulations, obligations and agreements by or on behalf of and
other provisions for the benefit of the Corporation, the District or the Escrow Agent contained in
this Escrow Agreement:
(1)

Shall bind and inure to the benefit of any such successor, and

(2)
Shall bind and inure to the benefit of any officer, board, authority,
agent or instrumentality to whom or to which there shall be transferred by or in
accordance with law any relevant right, power or duty of the Corporation or the Escrow
Agent, respectively, or of its successor.

BOARD OF DIRECTORS REPORT
Committee Meeting Date:
2026 Debt Service Defeasance - FasTracks Bonds

November 11, 2025
Board Meeting Date:
December 2, 2025

RECOMMENDED ACTION
For the Board of Directors to approve defeasance of 2026 debt service for FasTracks Bonds.
STAFF REPRESENTATIVES
Kelly Mackey, Chief Financial Officer
Brenden Morgan, Director, Treasury
PRESENTATION LENGTH
10 minutes
BACKGROUND
The Five-Year Financial Forecast (FYFF) shows that maintaining net revenue coverage equal to or
greater than 1.2x as required by the Fiscal Policy will be challenging in the coming years. To create
relief for the net revenue coverage calculation for 2026, staff examined various financing options, one
of which was deferring and extending the repayment of certain debt service obligations, commonly
referred to as “scoop and toss,” to reduce debt service payments during 2026. After a rigorous
examination, staff and external advisors determined that the costs of executing this option in a manner
that is helpful for 2026, which would include the repayment of such borrowing over a subsequent fiveyear period, would likely exceed $5 million.
A more efficient option that has an equally beneficial impact on debt service and net revenue coverage
in 2026, without the additional increased interest cost is the prepayment in 2025 of certain debt
obligations due and payable in 2026. This technique is referred to as defeasing a debt obligation to
maturity.
A defeasance is a financial technique in which an issuer sets aside cash in an irrevocable escrow held
by a financial institution (typically the related bond trustee) to cover, together with investment earnings,
future principal and interest payments on an existing obligation. The cash is invested in U.S.
Government Treasury Bonds maturing prior to the need to fund scheduled payments of principal and
interest on the defeased obligations. Bondholders are paid all due principal and interest on the
scheduled payment dates from funds deposited in the escrow account, and bondholders can only look
to the escrow for payment. This process discharges the issuer's payment obligation for the defeased
obligations, allowing those debt obligations to be removed from the issuer's balance sheet for financial
reporting purposes, even though the original debt remains outstanding until the escrow fully repays the

Packet Pg. 220

1.D.6

obligation on its payment date. This is a technique that RTD has used in the past when refunding or
refinancing debt.
In 2026, RTD is scheduled to make the following principal and interest payments:
FasTracks Bonds, Series 2022AB
Principal: $12,130,000
Interest: $9,971,810
Total: $22,101,810
DISCUSSION
The proposed Five-Year Financial Forecast and proposed 2026 budget were developed with the
assumption that RTD would execute a defeasance of $57,277,185, which includes that identified above.
Without executing this defeasance, operating expense would need to be reduced in 2026 if the budget
were to remain compliant with the 1.2x net revenue coverage ratio requirement of the Fiscal Policy.
Staff has engaged RTD’s bond counsel, Hogan Lovells; financial advisor, Hilltop Securities; bond
trustee, Bank of New York; and a verification agent, Causey, Demgen & Moore, to assist with
developing the attached documents which will be used if RTD moves forward with this bond
defeasance. The documents include an RTD resolution for bond payment defeasance and an escrow
agreement.
FINANCIAL IMPACT
Executing this defeasance in 2025 would allow the 2026 budget to remain compliant with the Fiscal
Policy requirement to maintain a net revenue coverage ratio of 1.2x based on revenue and expense in
the 2026 Proposed Budget that was posted for public inspection on October 10, 2025.

(except certain alternative minimum taxes described in bond counsel's opinion), and in any event
in such a manner so as not to increase the price paid for the initial acquisition of Federal
Securities for the Escrow Account. The certified public accountant's report must indicate that the
receipts from the substitute securities are sufficient without any need for reinvestment to fully
pay the Defeased Bond Payment Requirements. In lieu of, or in addition to, substituting other
Federal Securities pursuant to the preceding sentence, moneys in an amount equal to the
principal of and interest on all or any portion of such Initial Federal Securities may be credited to
the Escrow Account subject to the provisions of Section 5 hereof. Any such cash shall be
deemed to be part of the initial deposit. Any Federal Securities temporarily substituted may be
withdrawn from the Escrow Account when the Initial Federal Securities are purchased and
credited to the Escrow Account. Similarly, any temporary advancement of moneys to the
Escrow Account to pay designated Defeased Bond Payment Requirements, because of a failure
to receive promptly the principal of and interest on any Federal Securities at their respective
fixed maturity dates, or otherwise, may be repaid to the person advancing such moneys upon the
receipt by the Escrow Agent of such principal and interest payments on such Federal Securities.
If the Escrow Agent learns that the Department of the Treasury or the Bureau of
Fiscal Service will not, for any reason, accept a subscription of SLGS that is to be submitted
pursuant to this Agreement, the Escrow Agent shall promptly request alternative written
investment instructions from the District with respect to funds which were to be invested in
SLGS. The Escrow Agent shall follow such instructions and, upon the maturity of any such
alternative investment, the Escrow Agent shall hold such funds uninvested and without liability
for interest until receipt of further written instructions from the District. In the absence of
investment instructions from the District, the Escrow Agent shall not be responsible for the
investment of such funds or interest thereon. The Escrow Agent may conclusively rely upon the
District’s selection of an alternative investment as a determination of the alternative investment's
legality and suitability and shall not be liable for any losses related to the alternative investments
or for compliance with any yield restriction applicable thereto.
C.
The initial deposit, the proceeds of the Initial Federal Securities (and of
any other Federal Securities acquired as an investment or reinvestment of moneys accounted for
in the Escrow Account), and any such Federal Securities themselves (other than Federal
Securities, including the Initial Federal Securities, held as book-entries) shall be deposited with
the Escrow Agent and credited to and accounted for in the Escrow Account. The securities and
moneys accounted for therein shall be redeemed and paid out and otherwise administered by the
Escrow Agent for the benefit of the District and the owners of the 2022A/B Bonds as provided in
this Escrow Agreement and the Indenture.
-3-

Attachment: 2026 Debt Service Defeasance - FasTracks Bonds - Escrow Agreement (5228 : 2026 Debt Service Defeasance - FasTracks Bonds)

1.D.6.b

Packet Pg. 234

Section 2.

Purpose of Escrow.

A.
The Escrow Agent shall hold the initial deposit, all Federal Securities
accounted for in the Escrow Account (other than any Federal Securities, including the Initial
Federal Securities, held as book-entries), and all moneys received from time to time as interest
on and principal of such Federal Securities (including those held as book-entries), in trust to
secure and for the payment of the Defeased Bond Payment Requirements, as the same become
due.
B.
Except as provided in paragraph B of Section 1 and in Section 8 hereof,
the Escrow Agent shall collect the principal of and interest on such Federal Securities promptly
as such principal and interest become due and shall apply all money so collected to the payment
of the Defeased Bond Payment Requirements as aforesaid.
Section 3.

Accounting for Escrow.

A.
The moneys and the Federal Securities accounted for in the Escrow
Account shall not be subject to checks drawn by the District or otherwise subject to the order of
the District except as otherwise provided in paragraph B of Section 1 and in Section 8 hereof.
B.
From amounts on deposit in the Escrow Account, the Escrow Agent shall
make the transfers required by Section 7 hereof to permit the payment, without any default, of
the Defeased Bond Payment Requirements as the same become due.
C.
Except as otherwise provided in paragraph B of Section 1 hereof, there
shall be no sale of any Federal Securities held hereunder, and no Federal Securities held
hereunder and callable for prior redemption at the District's option shall be called at any time for
prior redemption, except if necessary to avoid a default in the payment of the Defeased Bond
Payment Requirements.
Section 4.

Maturities of Federal Securities.

A.
Federal Securities shall not be callable by the issuer thereof and shall be
purchased in such manner:
(1)
So that such Federal Securities may be redeemed in due season at
their respective maturities to meet the Defeased Bond Payment Requirements as the same
become due; and
(2)
So that any sale or prior redemption of such Federal Securities
shall be unnecessary.
B.
There shall be no substitution of any Federal Securities except as
otherwise provided in paragraph B of Section 1 hereof.

-4-

Attachment: 2026 Debt Service Defeasance - FasTracks Bonds - Escrow Agreement (5228 : 2026 Debt Service Defeasance - FasTracks Bonds)

1.D.6.b

Packet Pg. 235

Section 5.

Reinvestments.

A.
The Escrow Agent shall reinvest the cash balances listed in Exhibit 1
(including Exhibit A therein) for the period designated therein, if any, in state and local
government series securities (“SLGS”) purchased directly from the United States Government by
the Escrow Agent in the name of the District. All of the SLGS in which such reinvestments are
made shall bear interest at the rate of zero percent (0%) per annum. The Escrow Agent agrees to
comply with Part 344 of Title 31, Code of Federal Regulations, and with such other regulations
of the United States Treasury, Bureau of Public Debt, as are from time to time in effect in
subscribing for and purchasing such SLGS, including without limitation, requirements with
respect to submitting subscriptions to a Federal Reserve Bank or Branch in advance of the date
of purchase of the SLGS.
B.
In addition to or, as the case may be, in lieu of the reinvestments required
by paragraph A of this Section, the Escrow Agent, at the written direction of the District, shall
invest the initial cash, if any, and shall reinvest in Federal Securities any moneys received in
payment of the principal of and interest on any Federal Securities accounted for in the Escrow
Account. The District’s direction shall be subject to the limitations of Sections 1, 4 and 6 hereof
and the following limitations. In providing written direction to the Escrow Agent, the District
certifies that the investment does not fail to comply with any limitations of Sections 1, 4, 6, or as
follows:
(1)
Any such Federal Securities shall not be subject to redemption
prior to their respective maturities at the option of their issuer.
(2)
Any such Federal Securities shall mature on or prior to the date
when the proceeds thereof must be available for the prompt payment of the Defeased
Bond Payment Requirements, as the same become due.
(3)
Under no circumstances shall any reinvestment be made under this
Section if such reinvestment, alone or in combination with any other investment or
reinvestment, violates the applicable provisions of Section 148 of the Tax Code, and the
rules and regulations thereunder.
(4)
The District shall have furnished to the Escrow Agent a written
opinion of the District's bond counsel to the effect that such reinvestment, as described in
the opinion, will not adversely affect the federal tax treatment of interest on the 2022A/B
Bonds, and a verification report of an independent accountant or verification agent to the
effect that, after such reinvestment, the securities and funds in the Escrow Account shall
remain sufficient to make the payments of the Defeased Bond Payment Requirements as
they become due and payable.
Section 6.
Sufficiency of Escrow. The moneys and Federal Securities
accounted for in the Escrow Account shall be in an amount (or have appropriate maturities and
yields to produce an amount) which at all times shall be sufficient to pay the Defeased Bond
Payment Requirements as they become due.
-5-

Attachment: 2026 Debt Service Defeasance - FasTracks Bonds - Escrow Agreement (5228 : 2026 Debt Service Defeasance - FasTracks Bonds)

1.D.6.b

Packet Pg. 236

Section 7.
Transfers for Defeased Bond Payment Requirements. The
Escrow Agent shall make such credit arrangements and transfers to the trustee for the 2022A/B
Bonds (the “Trustee”) as will assure, to the extent of money in the Escrow Account properly
allocable to and available therefor, the timely payment of the Defeased Bond Payment
Requirements when due. The Escrow Agent shall not be responsible for the sufficiency of the
Escrow Account.
Section 8.
Termination of Escrow Account. When payment or provisions
for payment shall have been made so that all Defeased Bond Payment Requirements shall have
been paid in full and discharged, the Escrow Agent shall immediately pay over to the District the
moneys, if any, then remaining in the Escrow Account and shall make forthwith a final report to
the District. Such moneys may be used by the District for any lawful purpose, subject to any
limitations in the Indenture.
Section 9.

Fees.

A.
The Escrow Agent's total fees and ordinary costs for and in carrying out
the provisions of this Escrow Agreement have been fixed at $1,000.00, which amount is to be
paid at or prior to the date hereof directly to the Escrow Agent as payment in full of all charges
of the Escrow Agent pertaining to this Escrow Agreement for services performed hereunder. In
addition, the District shall pay and/or reimburse the Escrow Agent for its reasonable
extraordinary costs incurred hereunder, including, without limitation, its reasonable legal fees
and expenses.
B.
Such payment for services rendered and to be rendered by the Escrow
Agent shall not be for deposit in the Escrow Account, and the fees of and the costs incurred by
the Escrow Agent shall not be deducted from such account.
Section 10.

Character of Deposit.

A.
It is recognized that title to the Federal Securities and money accounted
for in the Escrow Account from time to time shall remain vested in the District or in the Escrow
Agent on behalf of the District but subject always to the prior charge and lien thereon of this
Escrow Agreement and the use thereof required to be made by the provisions of this Escrow
Agreement and the Indenture.
B.
The Escrow Agent shall hold all such Federal Securities (except as they
may be held as book-entries) and money in the Escrow Account as a special escrow fund, which
is accounted for separately and shall never commingle such securities or money with other
securities or money in non-trust areas of the Escrow Agent.
Section 11.

Securing Deposit.

A.
The Escrow Agent may cause the Federal Securities accounted for in the
Escrow Account to be registered in the name of the Escrow Agent on behalf of the District for
payment, if they are registrable for payment, and in such event shall obtain the necessary
endorsements from the duly authorized officials of the District as they become due.

any uninvested moneys accounted for in the Escrow Account may from time to time be placed

such transfer the District consents thereto in writing.
F.
Each such trust bank holding any Federal Securities accounted for in the
Escrow Account or any uninvested moneys accounted for therein shall be furnished by the
Escrow Agent with a copy of this Escrow Agreement prior to such deposit.

Notices.

The Escrow Agent, on behalf of the District, shall, as soon as practicable
following the defeasance of the Defeased Bond Payments, provide or cause to be provided notice
of the defeasance of the Defeased Bond Payments to the extent required in accordance with the
Indenture. The form of such notice of defeasance is attached hereto as Exhibit 2.
Section 13.

Irrevocability and Amendment.

A.
Except as herein provided this Escrow Agreement shall be irrevocable and
not subject to amendment.
B.
The provisions of this Escrow Agreement may be amended, waived or
modified upon approval of the owners of all of the then outstanding 2022A/B Bonds. The
provisions of this Escrow Agreement also may be amended, waived or modified without the
approval of such owners for one or more of the following purposes:
(1)
to cure any ambiguity, or to cure, correct or supplement any formal

purposes, or that any instrument executed hereunder complies with the conditions and provisions
of this Section.
Section 14.

Exculpatory Provisions.

A.
The duties and responsibilities of the Escrow Agent are limited to those
expressly and specifically stated in this Escrow Agreement.
B.
The Escrow Agent shall not be liable or responsible for any loss resulting
from any investment or reinvestment made pursuant to this Escrow Agreement and made in
compliance with the provisions hereof.
C.
The Escrow Agent shall not be liable for any act done or step taken or
omitted by it or for any mistake of fact or law or for anything which it may do or refrain from
doing, except for its gross negligence or willful misconduct.
D.
The Escrow Agent shall neither be under any obligation to inquire into or
be in any way responsible for the performance or nonperformance by the District of any of its
obligations contained in this Escrow Agreement, nor shall the Escrow Agent be responsible in
any manner for the recitals or statements in the Resolution, in the Indenture, in the 2022A/B
Bonds, or in any proceedings taken in connection therewith (other than its responsibilities as
trustee under such instruments.
E.
Nothing in this Escrow Agreement creates any obligation or liabilities on
the part of the Escrow Agent to anyone other than the District, the District and the owners of the
2022A/B Bonds.
F.
The Escrow Agent shall not be liable for the accuracy of the calculations
in the certified public accountant's report as to the sufficiency of the proceeds of the Federal
Securities and moneys to pay the Defeased Bond Payment Requirements. So long as the Escrow
Agent applies the proceeds of the Federal Securities and moneys held in the Escrow Account and
timely gives or causes the notices of defeasance to be given as provided herein, the Escrow

Agent shall not be liable for any deficiencies in the amounts necessary to pay the Defeased Bond

absence of its gross negligence or willful misconduct, the Escrow Agent may rely conclusively

J.

anything herein to the contrary notwithstanding.

Section 19. Electronic Transactions and Instructions. The parties hereto
agree that the transactions described herein may be conducted and related documents may be
stored by electronic means. Copies, electronic files and other reproductions of original executed
documents shall be deemed to be authentic and valid counterparts of such original documents for
all purposes, including the filing of any claim, action or suit in the appropriate court of law.
"Electronic means" shall mean the following communications methods: e-mail, secure electronic
transmission containing applicable authorization codes, passwords and/or authentication keys
issued by the Escrow Agent, or another method or system specified by the Escrow Agent as
available for use in connection with its services hereunder.
The Escrow Agent shall have the right to accept and act upon instructions, including funds
transfer instructions (“Instructions”) given pursuant to this Escrow Agreement and delivered
using electronic means; provided, however, that the District, as applicable, shall provide to the
Escrow Agent an incumbency certificate listing officers with the authority to provide such
Instructions (“Authorized Officers”) and containing specimen signatures of such Authorized
Officers, which incumbency certificate shall be amended by the District, as applicable, whenever
a person is to be added or deleted from the listing. If the District, as applicable, elects to give the
Escrow Agent Instructions using electronic means and the Escrow Agent in its discretion elects
to act upon such Instructions, the Escrow Agent’s understanding of such Instructions shall be
deemed controlling. The District understand and agree that the Escrow Agent cannot determine
the identity of the actual sender of such Instructions and that the Escrow Agent shall
conclusively presume that directions that purport to have been sent by an Authorized Officer
listed on the incumbency certificate provided to the Escrow Agent have been sent by such
Authorized Officer. The District shall be responsible for ensuring that only Authorized Officers
transmit such Instructions to the Escrow Agent and that the District and all Authorized Officers
are solely responsible to safeguard the use and confidentiality of applicable user and
authorization codes, passwords and/or authentication keys upon receipt by the District, as
applicable. The Escrow Agent shall not be liable for any losses, costs or expenses arising directly
or indirectly from the Escrow Agent’s reliance upon and compliance with such Instructions
notwithstanding such directions conflict or are inconsistent with a subsequent written instruction.
The District agree: (i) to assume all risks arising out of the use of electronic means to submit
Instructions to the Escrow Agent, including without limitation the risk of the Escrow Agent
acting on unauthorized Instructions, and the risk of interception and misuse by third parties; (ii)
that it is fully informed of the protections and risks associated with the various methods of
transmitting Instructions to the Escrow Agent and that there may be more secure methods of
transmitting Instructions than the method(s) selected by the District, as applicable; (iii) that the
security procedures (if any) to be followed in connection with its transmission of Instructions
provide to it a commercially reasonable degree of protection in light of its particular needs and

circumstances; and (iv) to notify the Escrow Agent immediately upon learning of any

Section 20. Bank Removal or Resignation. It is understood that the Escrow
Agent reserves the right to resign at any time by giving written notice of its resignation,
specifying the effective date thereof, to the District and that the District reserves the right to
remove the Escrow Agent at any time by giving written notice of its removal, specifying the
effective date thereof, to the Escrow Agent. Within 30 days after receipt of either of the
aforesaid notice, the District agrees to appoint a successor to which the Escrow Agent shall
transfer the deposits then held and all records pertaining thereto to such successor. If a successor
has not been appointed and has not accepted such appointment by the end of the 30-day period,
the Escrow Agent may apply, at the expense of the District, to a State of Colorado district court
with competent jurisdiction for the appointment of a bank or other financial institution
experienced in such matters as successor and the Escrow Agent shall transfer the deposits then
held and all records pertaining thereto to such successor.
Section 21. Governing Law. This Agreement shall be interpreted and
enforced in accordance with and governed by the laws of the State of Colorado.

similar securities which are direct obligations of, or obligations the principal of and interest on
which are unconditionally guaranteed by, the United States of America to pay and discharge all
of the principal (consisting of mandatory sinking fund redemption payments) and interest due
and payable in calendar year 2026 on the District's Taxable (Convertible to Tax-Exempt) Sales
Tax Revenue Bonds (FasTracks Project), Series 2022A (the "2022A Bonds"), and its Taxable
(Convertible to Tax-Exempt) Sales Tax Revenue Bonds (FasTracks Project), Series 2022B (the
"2022B Bonds" and together with the 2022A Bonds, the "2022A/B Bonds") as more particularly
described below.
B.

and interest due and payable in calendar year 2026 on the 2022A/B Bonds, as further described

BOARD OF DIRECTORS REPORT
Committee Meeting Date:
Long-Range Financial Plan

November 11, 2025
Board Meeting Date:
December 2, 2025

RECOMMENDED ACTION
For the Board of Directors to approve the Long-Range Financial Plan.
STAFF REPRESENTATIVES
Kelly Mackey, Chief Financial Officer
Todd Nikkel, Senior Manager, Budget
Brian Welch, Senior Manager, Planning Technical Services
PRESENTATION LENGTH
10 minutes
BACKGROUND
The Long-Range Financial Plan serves as an extension of the Five-Year Financial Forecast (FYFF)
through the 30-year time horizon, which is currently 2055. This plan is submitted to the Denver
Regional Council of Governments (DRCOG), the federally designated metropolitan planning
organization for the Denver region pursuant to the Federal Transit Act, 23 U.S.C. 5301, et seq. DRCOG
will incorporate RTD’s plan along with the plans of other member governments and partners in the
Regional Transportation Plan (RTP) that is updated every four years as required by 23 CFR § 450.324 in
order for projects to receive federal funding. The RTP guides the long-range vision and investment
framework for the region’s multimodal transportation system. DRCOG relies on financial forecasts
developed by RTD to determine the amount of funding available for use in RTD’s transit network. RTD’s
lenders also utilize the plan to ensure that RTD has the financial capacity to repay its debt.
DISCUSSION
The Long-Range Financial Plan focuses on evaluating whether RTD can fund the ongoing operation and
maintenance of the Base System and the FasTracks corridors while repaying its debt obligations. Key
elements of the plan for the years 2026-2055 include the following:
•

Revenue Projections
o Sales-and-use tax forecasts from the September 2025 forecast from the Leeds School of
Business at the University of Colorado Boulder
o Fare revenue forecasts based on the current pricing structure, $0.25 increases every three
years (a change previously indicated in the Discussion Item) and existing fare check
strategy with DRCOG ridership projections
o Future formula grants forecast based on historic appropriations, escalated at the
Consumer Price Index (CPI)

Packet Pg. 249

1.D.7

•

•

•

Operations and Capital Replacement
o Continued operating costs based on the final year of the FYFF, escalated at 3% CPI with
vehicle, hour and mile adjustments for increased transit utilization
o Replacement of revenue fleet and other assets based on current asset inventory and
replacement schedules
o Replacement of maintenance facilities as projected to be required
o Issuance of additional Certificates of Participation (COPs) in the FYFF to fund a portion of
capital replacement requirements
o Any incremental costs (capital and operations) for DRCOG RTP bus rapid transit (BRT)
corridors above those funding levels currently provided by RTD that would be paid for
and financed by stakeholder project sponsors
Reserves
o A balance of three months’ operating expenses in the Board-appropriated operating
reserve
o Short-term use of FasTracks Internal Savings Account (FISA) to fund FasTracks state of
good repair efforts in the FYFF
o Reserves fully utilized with a gap between revenue projections and expenditure
requirements
Other Assumptions Beyond the FYFF
o That the Concession Agreement with Denver Transit Operators for the A, B, and G Lines
remains in place through 2044, with RTD assuming operations thereafter
o That the entire light rail system will be converted to level boarding
o That a new bus operating facility will be built or acquired
o That a new light rail operating facility located in the eastern portion of the light rail
system will be built
o That the existing Automatic Block Signals System for light rail is converted to a
Communication-Based Train Control (CBTC) Moving Block Signal System
o That the agency does not assume ownership of private contractor bus operations
facilities

The Long-Range Financial Plan does not incorporate proposed defeasance of a portion of 2026 debt
obligations.
Implementation of the Facilities and Fleet Transition Plan would add approximately $1.4B to the capital
costs above what is listed in the Long-Range Financial Plan schedules. Due to complexities and
unknowns in the fleet replacement schedules, the Facilities and Fleet Transition Plan is not able to be
incorporated into the Long-Range Financial Plan by year at this time.
FINANCIAL IMPACT
The recommended Long-Range Financial Plan does not provide RTD with the means to maintain its
current system in a state of good repair through 2055. Between 2026 and 2055, RTD would not have the
capacity for service expansion or new projects beyond those needed to maintain a state of good repair,
and the FISA alone would not be sufficient to fund the unfunded FasTracks corridors.

Packet Pg. 250

1.D.7

Unrestricted funds and capital replacement reserves are fully utilized by 2031 for the existing
infrastructure state of good repair. Additional debt issuance and revenue is required in the Long-Range
Financial Plan.

BOARD OF DIRECTORS REPORT
Committee Meeting Date:
July 2025 Five-Year Financial Forecast

November 11, 2025
Board Meeting Date:
December 2, 2025

RECOMMENDED ACTION
For the Board of Directors to adopt the July 2025 Five-Year Financial Forecast
STAFF REPRESENTATIVE
Kelly Mackey, Chief Financial Officer
Todd Nikkel, Senior Manager, Budget
PRESENTATION LENGTH
20 minutes
BACKGROUND
The July 2025 Five-Year Financial Forecast (FYFF) for 2026-2030 is the financial forecast used as the
basis for the development of the 2026 Proposed Budget and provides guidance for future years’
financial planning.
The development of the FYFF seeks to balance planned expenditures with anticipated available funding
sources in alignment with RTD’s Strategic Plan. The FYFF is prepared on an annual basis or can be
produced more frequently if material changes in assumptions and inputs occur. The previous financial
forecast, the 2025-2029 FYFF, was approved by the Board in September 2024.
The FYFF was prepared using currently available information to assist in planning. The FYFF is a
forecast or projection of financial results, is not an appropriation of funds, and is non-binding.
During the July 15, 2025, Finance and Planning Committee, staff presented a discussion item that
described the purpose of and assumptions used in the FYFF. During the September 9, 2025, Finance
and Planning Committee, staff presented an action item for adoption of the 2026-2030 FYFF, which was
approved. The Board of Directors voted on September 30, 2025, to return the action item to the Finance
and Planning Committee meeting for further review.
DISCUSSION
The FYFF has been prepared using currently available information and does not include assumptions
regarding future potential changes, such as new grant funding from SB24-184 Congestion Impact Fees
and SB24-230 Oil and Gas Production Fees. The FYFF only includes funding sources and use
projections that have reasonable certainty to occur in accordance with RTD’s Board-approved Fiscal
Policy.

Packet Pg. 256

1.D.8

Other requirements of the Fiscal Policy to consider for the FYFF include the following:
•
•

A balanced budget in which beginning reserves plus total anticipated revenues is greater
than or equal to expenditures will be prepared
Debt financing will not be issued to support operating expenditures

FINANCIAL IMPACT
The FYFF projects continued adherence to Fiscal Policy requirements and maintenance of adequate
reserves to continue to cash-fund expenditures while providing the necessary funding to support
currently known Transit Asset Management Plan needs.

BOARD OF DIRECTORS DISCUSSION ITEM
Committee Meeting Date:
Triennial Update to Reimagine RTD – Mobility Plan for the
Future

November 11, 2025

STAFF REPRESENTATIVE
Brian Welch, Senior Manager, Planning Technical Services
Bill Sirois, Senior Manager, Transit Oriented Communities
PRESENTATION LENGTH
15 minutes
BACKGROUND
In 2018, RTD recognized that the landscape of surface transportation was in a state of flux and put in
motion several complementary efforts and initiatives. These efforts were collectively referred to as
“Transportation Transformation” and included the following vision:
•
•
•

Transit systems need to make themselves more competitive now
It is time for a public transportation renaissance
The future of mobility depends on public transportation: practical, sustainable solutions that
meet the needs of everyone in the Denver metro area

The signature Transportation Transformation initiative became the Reimagine RTD project, and work
began in late 2019 to develop the Mobility Plan for the Future (MPFF) and the System Optimization Plan
(SOP). The SOP was adopted by the Board in July 2022, and a Board SOP update was presented in
September 2025. The Board endorsed the MPFF in November of 2022, with the understanding that the
MPFF would be reviewed and updated on a no-less-than triennial basis.
DISCUSSION
The overarching Reimagine RTD aspiration is as follows: “Moving everyone forward with solutions.”
Key highlights of the MPFF are presented by four opportunities, describing RTD as follows:
•
•
•
•

Access: A mobility integrator that provides a regional transit backbone and partners with
stakeholders
Equity: A mobility provider prioritizing service to those most in need
Sustainability: A mobility leader that defines and evolves transit’s role through innovation and
collaboration
Financial: A mobility agency that is well-funded, financially stable, and serves as a good steward
of taxpayer dollars while supporting regional access, equity, and sustainability

Note that these opportunities are harmonized with the strategic priorities and success outcomes
described in the 2021-2026 Strategic Plan. The attached presentation also includes a three-year update

Packet Pg. 270

1.E.1

to the MPFF implementation plan, which is linked to the Strategic Plan and is organized on a temporal
and financial basis. Key implementation steps include the following:
•
•
•
•
•
•
•

Implement a partnership program (the MPFF meets the Community Value Strategic Priority)
Collaborate with CDOT/local partners to implement regional Bus Rapid Transit (BRT) service (the
MPFF meets the Community Value Strategic Priority)
Develop a zero-emission fleet transition plan (the MPFF meets the Community Value Strategic
Priority)
Integrate services and modes through development of a trip planning and payment platform (the
MPFF meets the Customer Excellence Strategic Priority)
Continue to foster a dynamic, diverse workforce that attracts and retains valued people (the
MPFF meets the Employee Ownership Strategic Priority)
Continue to seek opportunities to enhance transit safety (the MPFF meets the Community Value
Strategic Priority)
Initiate a formal effort to collaborate with state and local partners to increase transit funding in
the region (the MPFF meets the Financial Success Strategic Priority)

Moving forward in 2026 and beyond, key long-range planning initiatives related to the MPFF include:
•
•
•
•
•

Light Rail Level-Boarding Feasibility Study
New Bus Maintenance Facility Alternative Analysis (AA) and National Environmental Policy Act
(NEPA) Study
Bus Stop Infrastructure Accessibility Assessment
Park-n-Ride Assessment
Comprehensive Operational Analysis (COA)

Setting long-range planning priorities for the agency beyond the current MPFF will occur using the COA
as a cornerstone. The COA will establish a five-year plan for service and develop aspirations for service
beyond five years, both of which are contingent upon funding. The COA will establish a baseline from
which the agency can build to determine long-term priorities for asset renewal and other infrastructure
investments related to system modernization and expansion. This process is expected to begin in 2027
following the completion of the COA.
FINANCIAL IMPACT
There is no financial impact associated with this Discussion Item.

2022 MPFF Expected Outcomes
§ Focus RTD’s resources on regional services that would be difficult for local agencies to
provide

§ Increase involvement of local agencies in the provision of community-based services
§ Put RTD in the lead of developing a customer-focused, regional trip planning and payment
integration platform

§ Better define RTD’s service priorities by focusing resources on high-demand corridors
and customers in need of service

§ Encourage RTD to lead mobility and climate action initiatives
§ Align RTD’s expenditures with anticipated resources

§ Initiate efforts to collaborate with state and local partners to

• This funding is expected to be available beginning in 2026
